[?2004l
Usage:  docker container COMMAND

Manage containers

Commands:
  attach      Attach local standard input, output, and error streams to a running container
  commit      Create a new image from a container's changes
  cp          Copy files/folders between a container and the local filesystem
  create      Create a new container
  diff        Inspect changes to files or directories on a container's filesystem
  exec        Execute a command in a running container
  export      Export a container's filesystem as a tar archive
  inspect     Display detailed information on one or more containers
  kill        Kill one or more running containers
  logs        Fetch the logs of a container
  ls          List containers
  pause       Pause all processes within one or more containers
  port        List port mappings or a specific mapping for the container
  prune       Remove all stopped containers
  rename      Rename a container
  restart     Restart one or more containers
  rm          Remove one or more containers
  run         Create and run a new container from an image
  start       Start one or more stopped containers
  stats       Display a live stream of container(s) resource usage statistics
  stop        Stop one or more running containers
  top         Display the running processes of a container
  unpause     Unpause all processes within one or more containers
  update      Update configuration of one or more containers
  wait        Block until one or more containers stop, then print their exit codes

Run 'docker container COMMAND --help' for more information on a command.

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Run  a process in a new container. [1mdocker[0m [1mrun[0m starts a process with its[m
       own file system, its own networking, and its own isolated process tree.[m
[7m Manual page docker-run(1) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K       The  IMAGE  which starts the process may define defaults related to the[m
       process that will be run in the container, the  networking  to  expose,[m

       istrator who starts the container  from  the  image.  For  that  reason[m
       [1mdocker[0m [1mrun[0m has more options than any other Docker command.[m

       [1m--entrypoint[0m=""[m
          Overwrite the default ENTRYPOINT of the image[m
[m
       This option allows you to overwrite the default entrypoint of the image[m
       that is set in the Dockerfile. The ENTRYPOINT of an image is similar to[m
[7m Manual page docker-run(1) line 273 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       a COMMAND because it specifies what executable to  run  when  the  conâ€[m
       tainer  starts,  but  it is (purposely) more difficult to override. The[m
       ENTRYPOINT gives a container its default nature or  behavior,  so  that[m
       when you set an ENTRYPOINT you can run the container as if it were that[m
       binary, complete with default options, and you can pass in more options[m
       via  the  COMMAND. But, sometimes an operator may want to run something[m
       else inside the container, so you can override the  default  ENTRYPOINT[m
       at  runtime by using a [1m--entrypoint[0m and a string to specify the new ENâ€[m
       TRYPOINT.[m
